)@@G@@)     @C@@@@       4. RLIB$1 (CREATED BY RLIB$O - SEE BELOW)@C@@@@      MJ

)@@G@@ND BOOT TAPES SEPARATE:  AS MENTIONED ABOVE, IT @F@@@@ WAS ONLY NECESSARMN
)@@G@@Y TO SWITCH THE PLUGS AT 'ENTER DATE' TIME.     @F@@@@ HOWEVER, THINGS BMO
)@@G@@ECOME A BIT MORE DIFFICULT ON LEVEL 31, SINCE   @F@@@@ AN EXTRA FILE EXIMP
)@@G@@STS ON THE BOOT TAPE (THE COLLECTOR DIAGNOSTIC  @G@@@@ FILE FOR THE PANIMQ
)@@G@@C DUMP ANALYZER'S USE).  ON A NO-SWITCH TAPE BOOT,    @F@@@@ THIS PROVIDMR
)@@G@@ES NO PROBLEM, SINCE THE BOOT TAPE IS STILL UP, BUT ON@B@@@@ A SWITCH 4 MS
)@@G@@BOOT, THE FOLLOWING HAPPENS:  @[@@@@SPACE @E@@@@       1. THE DIAGNOSTICMT
)@@G@@ FILE AT POSITION 2 IS SKIPPED.     @B@@@@       2. THE LIBRARIES ARE COMU
)@@G@@PIED IN.    @F@@@@       3. THE SECOND COPY OF THE DIAGNOSTIC FILE IS COMV
)@@G@@PIED IN.    @[@@@@SPACE @F@@@@      WE MODIFIED THE ELEMENT INDA TO AVOIMW
)@@G@@D SKIPPING THE FIRST    @F@@@@ COPY OF THE DIAGNOSTIC FILE, SINCE WE AREMX
)@@G@@ ALREADY POSITIONED AT  @E@@@@ LIB$1.  THE 'SYS' RUNSTREAM IN SYS$*RUN$.MY
)@@G@@BOOTELT WAS THEN  @F@@@@ CHANGED TO DO THE FOLLOWING AFTER THE LIBRARIESMZ
)@@G@@ ARE READ IN:     @[@@@@SPACE @A@@@@       1. @REWIND,I THE LIB TAPE.   NA
)@@G@@@E@@@@       2. DO A @MSG,W SAYING 'SWITCH BACK TO THE BOOT TAPE'.@E@@@@NB
)@@G@@       3. READ IN THE DIAGNOSTIC FILE FROM THE BOOT TAPE.   @[@@@@SPACE NC
)@@G@@@F@@@@      NOTE THAT THIS MAKES THE ASSUMPTION THAT THE BOOT TAPE HAS  ND
)@@G@@@E@@@@ BEEN LEFT POSITIONED WHERE THE BOOT PROCEDURE LEFT IT.     @^@@@@NE
)@@G@@427/31 COMPATIBILITY    @F@@@@      MOST OF OUR SYSTEMS PROCESSORS ARE NNF
)@@G@@OW COMPLETELY COMPATIBLE@F@@@@ WITH EITHER LEVEL 27 OR LEVEL 31, BUT THENG
)@@G@@ BOOT PROCEDURES HAVE   @F@@@@ CHANGED SO MUCH THAT WE HAVE ADDED A NEW NH
)@@G@@ELEMENT, 'BOOT31' TO    @G@@@@ SYS$*RUN$ AND CHANGED THE EXEC (ELEMENT INI
)@@G@@NDRIV) TO @ADD THAT INSTEAD   @G@@@@ OF 'BOOTELT' FOR THE TIME BEING, SINJ
)@@G@@NCE WE ARE DOING MUCH CROSSBOOTING. @F@@@@ THIS ENABLES USE TO USE THE SNK
)@@G@@AME LIBRARIES ON BOTH LEVELS, AND   @B@@@@ AVOIDS WASTING TIME WITH SWTINL
)@@G@@CH 4 BOOTS. @^@@@@4RUN$ IN @COPY,G FORMAT @G@@@@      IT'S NO SECRET THANM
)@@G@@T @COPIN TAKES AN AWFULLY LONG TIME, AND, IN    @F@@@@ THE CASE OF RLIB$NN
)@@G@@, THE @PREP CAN TAKE SEVERAL MINUTES.  THE EXEC @G@@@@ CHANGE NECESSARY NO
)@@G@@TO ALLOW THE RUN$ FILE TO BE IN @COPY,G FORMAT IS     @F@@@@ A SIMPLE ONNP
)@@G@@E TO INDRIV.  JUST CHANGE THE @COPIN STATEMENT IN THE @F@@@@ CANNED RUNSNQ
)@@G@@TREAM TO A @COPY,G.  CHANGING RLIB$ TO @COPY,G FORMAT,@C@@@@ HOWEVER, ISNR
)@@G@@ A DIFFERENT STORY (SEE BELOW).     @^@@@@4RLIB$ IN @COPY,G FORMAT@F@@@@NS
)@@G@@      FOR LIBRARY GENERATION PURPOSES, WE KEEP OUR FAST AND SLOW  @F@@@@NT
)@@G@@ RLIB$ FILES SEPARATE, IN FILES CALLED RLIB$FAST AND RLIB$SLOW.   @F@@@@NU
)@@G@@ ANY CHANGES TO THE LIBRARIES ARE MADE USING THESE FILES.  THE    @G@@@@NV
)@@G@@ LIBGEN SKELETON (ELSEWHERE IN THIS FILE) THEN PERFORMS THE FOLLOWING:  NW
)@@G@@@[@@@@SPACE @]@@@@COLUMN 7    @F@@@@   1. RLIB$FAST AND RLIB$SLOW ARE @PNX
)@@G@@ACK'ED IF THEY WERE CHANGED.  @D@@@@   2. A TEMPORARY FILE CALLED RLIB$TNY
)@@G@@EMP IS ASSIGNED.  @C@@@@   3. RLIB$FAST IS @COPY'ED INTO RLIB$TEMP.     NZ
)@@G@@@E@@@@   4. A @COPY,PC IS PERFORMED FROM RLIB$SLOW TO RLIB$TEMP.  @B@@@@OA
)@@G@@   5. RLIB$TEMP IS @PACK'ED AND @PREP'ED. @G@@@@   6. @RLIB$O (A SPECIALOB
)@@G@@ PROCESSOR WE WROTE) IS THEN CALLED TO WRITE    @E@@@@      THE FILE RLIOC
)@@G@@B$TEMP ONTO THE LIBTAPE IN THE FORM OF TWO@G@@@@      @COPY,G COMPATIBLEOD
)@@G@@ FILES.  THIS IS DONE BY WRITING A STANDARD     @G@@@@      COPYG LABEL OE
)@@G@@BLOCK, AND THEN COPYING X TRACKS OF RLIB$TEMP ONTO    @F@@@@      THE TAOF
)@@G@@PE, WHERE X IS THE CURRENT SIZE OF RLIB$FAST.  AN EOF @G@@@@      MARK IOG
)@@G@@S THEN WRITTEN, AND THE REST OF RLIB$TEMP IS COPIED ONTO    @D@@@@      OH
)@@G@@THE TAPE, PRECEDED AGAIN BY A COPYG LABEL BLOCK.@[@@@@SPACE @]@@@@COLUMNOI
)@@G@@ 2    @E@@@@ THE 'SYS' RUNSTREAM IN RUN$.BOOTELT ALSO HAD TO BE CHANGED.OJ
)@@G@@@F@@@@ THE @PREP OF RLIB$ WAS REMOVED, AND THE @COPIN'S WERE CHANGED    OK
)@@G@@@#@@@@ TO @COPY,G'S.    @E@@@@ THE EFFECT OF ALL THIS IS THAT, ON A SWITOL
)@@G@@CH 4 BOOT, RLIB$  @F@@@@ GETS COPIED IN MUCH QUICKER, AND DOESN'T HAVE TOM
)@@G@@O BE @PREP'ED.    @A@@@@4THE LIBGEN SKELETON AND PROCEDURES @F@@@@      ON
)@@G@@TWO SEPARATE LIBRARY GENERATION SKELETONS HAVE BEN CREATED. @F@@@@ THE FOO
)@@G@@IRST ONE, CALLED 'LIBGEN', USES THE CURRENT LIBRARY TAPE AS @F@@@@ INPUTOP
)@@G@@.  THE SECOND ONE, CALLED 'NEWLIB', USES THE CURRENTLY-     @F@@@@ CATALOQ
)@@G@@OGUED LIBRARY FILES (SYS$*LIB$, SYS$*RLIB$, ETC.) AS INPUT. @C@@@@ THE 'OR
)@@G@@LIBGEN' SKELETON WILL BE DESCRIBED FIRST. @#@@@@3'LIBGEN' SKELETON@E@@@@OS
)@@G@@      FIVE FILES ARE CREATED, CALLED LIB$1, LIB$2, RUN$,    @^@@@@ RLIB$OT
)@@G@@1, AND RLIB$2.    @F@@@@ THESE FILES SHOULD CONTAIN ONLY THE NEW OR UPDAOU
)@@G@@TED ITEMS TO BE   @^@@@@ ADDED IN THIS LIBRARY. @]@@@@ THE CURRENT@F@@@@OV
)@@G@@ LIBRARY TAPE IS USED AS INPUT: EACH FILE IS COPIED INTO TPF$,    @F@@@@OW
)@@G@@ THE PROPER FILE FROM THE LIST IS @COPY,PC'D INTO TPF$ ALSO, AND  @D@@@@OX

)@@G@@S MAY BE USED TO SPECIFY ELEMENTS TO BE DELETED, IF   @B@@@@ NO NEW ELEMOZ
)@@G@@ENT WITH THE SAME NAME/VERSION@C@@@@ IS PRESENT TO REPLACE IT.  ANY FILEPA

)@@G@@ TAPE.@D@@@@ LIB$1 AND LIB$2 WILL BE DONE VIA @COPIN:  ALL OTHERS @ @@@@PD

)@@G@@SPACE @D@@@@      THE 'FILES' SGS LISTS THE NAMES OF THE FILES    @F@@@@PH

)@@G@@IB' SKELETON@F@@@@     THIS SKELETON USES ONLY ONE TAPE AT A TIME, AND DPP

)@@G@@NTS OF LIB$ THAT SHOULD GO IN THE FAST LIB$ FILE, CALLED LIB$1.   @[@@@@PX
)@@G@@SPACE @F@@@@ FIVE SEPARATE TEMPORARY FILES ARE CREATED, SO THAT A TAPE-TPY

)@@G@@IB$1  @G@@@@ AND RLIB$2, THE CREATION, @PACK, AND @PREP OF RLIB$TEMP IS QA
)@@G@@BYPASSED,   @F@@@@ AND A @USE RLIB$TEMP,SYS$*RLIB$ IS DONE INSTEAD, ALLOQB
)@@G@@WING @RLIB$O@C@@@@ TO BE USED WHILE ELIMINATING MUCH OVERHEAD.    @]@@@@QC
)@@G@@4@EPDUP     @G@@@@      THE LIBGEN SKELETONS INCLUDE A CALL ON A PROGRAMQD
)@@G@@ CALLED @EPDUP,   @F@@@@ WHICH SEARCHES A PROGRAM FILE'S ENTRY POINT TABQE
)@@G@@LE FOR DUPLICATE  @F@@@@ ENTRIES.  IT IS USED ON THE RLIB$TEMP FILE TO CQF
)@@G@@HECK FOR POSSIBLE @]@@@@ ERRORS.    @]@@@@4@WATLIB    @G@@@@      THE @WQG
)@@G@@ATLIB PROCESSOR WAS WRITTEN TO LET USERS KEEP UP TO DATE    @G@@@@ ON EXQH
)@@G@@ACTLY WHAT LIBRARY CHANGES HAVE BEEN MADE, AND WHAT THE CURRENT   @]@@@@QI
)@@G@@ LIBRARY IS.@[@@@@SPACE @E@@@@      WHEN @WATLIB IS CALLED BY A USER, ITQJ
)@@G@@ DOES AN ER ID$   @E@@@@ (RESULT OF ANOTHER NYU SYSTEMS DEPT BRAINSTORM)QK
)@@G@@ TO PICK UP @E@@@@ THE EXEC LEVEL.  IT THEN GETS THE REST OF ITS INFORMAQL
)@@G@@TION  @F@@@@ FROM SYS$*RUN$.LIBLEVEL.  THIS ELEMENT IS CREATED BY THE LIQM
)@@G@@BGEN  @F@@@@ PROCEDURE.  THE FIRST LINE CONTAINS THE LIBRARY LEVEL NUMBEQN
)@@G@@R, AND@F@@@@ THE LIB TAPE NUMBERS.  (THE LIB TAPE NUMBERS ARE NOT PRINTEQO
)@@G@@D OUT @F@@@@ BY @WATLIB:  THEY ARE THERE FOR @WATLIB TO USE WHEN CALLED QP
)@@G@@BY THE@G@@@@ 'SYS' RUN DURING A BOOT.  AT THAT TIME, THE LIBLEVEL AND TAQQ
)@@G@@PE NUMBERS  @F@@@@ ARE GIVEN TO THE EXEC THROUGH ER ID$ SO THE 'C ID' KEQR
)@@G@@YIN CAN     @G@@@@ DISPLAY THEM.)  SYS$*RUN$.LIBLEVEL ALSO CONTAINS A LIQS
)@@G@@ST OF ALL THE     @G@@@@ CHANGES IN THE LIBRARY THAT MIGHT BE OF INTERESQT
)@@G@@T TO USERS.  THEY CAN   @B@@@@ GET FURTHER INFORMATION USING @NEWS.     QU
)@@G@@___ NEVER   @E@@@@ CHANGES, IS JUST COPIED FROM MASS STORAGE TO TAPE AFTQV
)@@G@@ER    @F@@@@ EVERYTHING ELSE IS DONE.  ANY ADDIT*[@@@@*SDFF*@#@@@@      QW
)@@G@@    AXR$    @[@@@@$(0)  @F@@@@B         'CSF$ ERROR'                  . QX
)@@G@@THIS STUFF WILL BE OVER-@G@@@@          +         0D                  . QY
